8  state law reference antiquities texas vtca natural resources   authority to preserve substandard building as historic property vtca local government purpose a the city council recognizes the historical cultural and aesthetic importance of certain buildings structures or districts within the city b the council desires to protect and preserve such landmarks and districts and such protection and preservation is in the best interests of both historical preservation and the citys economic wellbeing 01   designation of historic districts and landmarks a historic districts and historic landmarks the city council may from time to time designate certain areas in the city historic districts or certain places as historic landmarks those provisions pertaining to the designation of historic districts or historic landmarks constitute a part of the comprehensive zoning ordinance of the city all zoning maps shall reflect the historic district and landmark designation by the letter h as a suffix to the use designation b criteria in making the designation of an area or place as a historic district or landmark the city council shall consider one or more of the following criteria 1 character interest or value as part of the development heritage or cultural characteristics of the city  2 location as the site of a historical event  3 embodiment of distinguishing characteristics of an architectural type or specimen  4 relationship to other distinctive buildings sites districts or structures which are historically significant and preserved or which are eligible for preservation  5 unique location of singular physical characteristics representing an established and familiar visual feature of a neighborhood community or the city  6 value as an aspect of community sentiment or public pride  7 identification with a person who significantly contributed to the development or culture of the city  8 in the case of landmark designation the designation must be supported by the complete written consent of the property owner c downtown historic districts and designated landmarks 1 downtown historic district the city downtown area more specifically described below meets several of the aforesaid criteria and is hereby designated a historic district within the city beginning at the corner of second and e streets the district boundary follows e street northeast to fourth street  thence northwest to d street  thence northeast to fifth street  thence northwest to c street  thence northeast to the property line of baumann grocery  thence northwest to the corner of the baumann grocery property line  thence southwest to fifth street  thence northwest to b street  thence southwest crossing fourth street to the property line of stroziers paint and body shop  thence northwest to the corner of the stroziers paint and body shop  thence southwest to third street  thence northwest to the sanchez mrs annies property line  thence southwest to the comer of the sanchez mrs annies property line  thence southeast to b street  thence southeast to houston street and on next block to d street  thence northeast to second street  thence southeast to the point of origin at second and e street 2 future historic districts or landmarks future designation of additional areas or places as historic districts andor landmarks shall be governed by the further provisions of this section d submission to planning and zoning commission for future designations formal recommendations to the city or by the city for any additional area or location for district or landmark designation shall be submitted to the planning and zoning commission of the city within 30 days the commission shall give notice and conduct its hearing on the proposed designation such hearing shall be in the same manner and according to the same procedures as specifically provided for in the provisions of chapter 153 e uses nothing contained in this section or in the designation of property as being in a historic district or being a historic landmark shall affect the present legal use of property use classifications as to all property which may be included in a historic district or historic landmark shall continue to be governed by the general zoning provisions of this chapter and the procedures therein established in no case however shall any use be permitted which requires the demolition razing remodeling or alteration of any buildings or structures in such a historic district or historic landmark so as to adversely affect the character of the district or historic landmark except upon compliance with the terms of this section 02   creation of historic review board a board and board membership there is hereby created a historic review board of the city hereinafter called the board consisting of five members appointed by the city council the board shall be comprised of the following 1 at least four citizens of the city  2 at least two members of the main street board so long as such board is a functioning entity  3 at least two owners of property within the designated historic district  4 at least one member of the wilson county historical society so long as such association is a functioning entity  5 the building official or his representative shall serve as secretary and ex officio member of the board b term of appointment each member of the board shall be appointed for a term of two years except that of the members of the first board to be appointed three shall be appointed to serve for two years and two for one year the term shall expire on january 1 of the appropriate year any vacancy on the board shall be filled by the city council for the remainder of the unexpired term any member of the board who fails to attend at least 75 percent of all regular meetings of the board within any 12month period shall be removed from the board unless such failure to attend was the result of illness or other acceptable excuse as determined by the city council c chairperson and vicechairperson of the board the chairperson and vicechairperson of the board shall be elected annually by a majority of the members of the board and shall serve a term of one year or until their successors are elected d duties of the board the board shall act in an advisory capacity only and shall have no power to bind the city by contract or otherwise through the review procedure provided herein it shall be the function of the board to advise the building official concerning all applications for review in historic districts or historic landmarks and perform any other advisory functions delegated by the city council e meetings the board shall meet monthly at a regularly scheduled time unless no necessary business needs to be conducted special meetings may be called upon request of the chairperson or the vicechairperson or upon written request of two members or upon notice from the building official that a matter requires the consideration of the board all meetings shall have advance notice posted in accordance with the texas open meetings law three members shall constitute a quorum and action taken at a meeting shall require the affirmative vote of a majority of the members present and voting at such meeting 03   historic preservation review and permit required a no person shall proceed to make alterations changes restorations demolitions or removals to the exterior of or upon any historic landmark of or upon any building or improvement within a historic district without first submitting his plans to the building official as hereinafter provided and securing a permit to proceed b a historic preservation review is necessary for any proposed alteration change restoration or removal of any architectural feature of the exterior of a building or structure including exterior signage and painting for any historically designated property under the provisions of this section application for historical preservation review shall be made to the building official regular building permit procedure of the city c nothing contained herein shall be construed as requiring the historical review process for any regular maintenance of any building that does not alter the exterior presentation or structure of the building d application shall be deemed complete when submitted upon city forms complete with drawings plans and specifications of when submitted upon a form and in a form otherwise acceptable to the building official e no charge or fee will be required for a historic preservation review but the review process while in conjunction with the building permit process does not relieve or take the place of building permit and fee requirements provided for elsewhere in this f historic preservation review acceptance however shall be a prerequisite to the issuance of a building permit 04   review process a if the building official determines that the application involves ordinary repair or maintenance or alteration change restoration or removal of any exterior architectural feature of a building structure or sign which does not involve significant changes in the architectural or historic value style general design or appearance he shall within seven days forward a copy of the application indicating the determination to the chairperson of the board or to the vicechairperson of the board if the chairperson is not available the chairperson or vicechairperson of the board shall within five business days either approve the building officials determination or call for a meeting of the board to consider the application as provided in subsection c of this section if the chairperson or vicechairperson of the board do not take any action within five business days it shall be deemed that the board shall take no action and the building official shall indicate the applications acceptance for historic review purposes on the building permit b if the building official determines that the application involves an alteration change restoration removal or demolition of an external architectural feature of a building or structure which involves a significant change in the architectural or historic value style general design or appearance he shall refer the application to the board and call for a meeting of the board to consider the application c the board shall hold a meeting to consider the application within 15 business days after the building officials receipt of a completed application the applicant shall be given written notice of the time and place of the meeting the board may hold any additional meetings it considers necessary to carry out its responsibilities under this section the board shall make its recommendation to the building official within 30 days after receipt of a completed application unless the board and the applicant mutually agree to extend the period of review d notwithstanding any other provision of this section the board shall make its recommendation to the building official within 90 days after receipt of complete application for a permit to demolish a historic landmark or a building within a historic district or to move a historic landmark or to move a building into or out of a historic district e the board shall forward its recommendation to the building official while the building official is not bound by such recommendation he shall within five business days of its receipt give written notice of the applications acceptance or denial such notice shall be deemed complete once filed with the city secretary or by issuance of a permit showing acceptance 1 in the case of applications that do not involve demolition of a historic building or landmark an application shall be deemed accepted if no notice of action by the building official is given within 60 days after the receipt of a completed application unless time has been mutually extended as provided above 2 in the case of applications that involve demolition of a historic building or landmark an application shall be deemed accepted if no notice of action by the building official is given within 100 days after the receipt of a completed application unless time has been mutually extended as provided above 05   criteria to be used in determining the recommendations and action on acceptance of an application for historic preservation review the building official and board shall consider the following 1 the effect of the proposed change upon the general historic cultural and architectural nature of the district or landmark  2 the appropriateness of exterior architectural features which can be seen from a public street alley or walkway  3 the general design arrangement texture material and color of the building or structure and the relation of such factors to similar features of buildings or structures in the district the criteria shall not be the aesthetic appeal to the board of the structure or the proposed remodeling but rather its conformity to the general character of the particular historic area involved  4 all signs shall be in keeping with the character of the historic district or landmark  5 the value of this historic district or landmark as an area of unique interest and character shall be impaired  6 the general and specific secretary of the interiors standards for rehabilitation and guidelines for applying the standards for rehabilitation  and 7 the importance of finding a way to meet the current needs of the property owner and the importance of approving plans that will be economically feasible for the property owner 06   appeal to city council any person aggrieved by an action of the board or building official relative to the acceptance or denial of an application shall have the right to appeal to the city council by giving notice of appeal within 15 days of such action the council shall sit as a review board an appeal hearing shall be set within 30 days of notice the council ruling may uphold overrule or modify the building officials decision 07   annual report a the board shall make an annual report to the city council on the state of historic preservation in the city and shall include in the report a summary of its activities for the past year and a proposed program for the next year b the board shall have the further responsibility of recommending to the city council planning and zoning commission and the city departments the adoption of policies the sources of funds and designation of historic districts and historic landmarks that may further the citys preservation effort 08   chapter 155  exemptions for political subdivisions definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this chapter shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning administrative fee means any fee charged by the city for the processing of requests relating to land usage including but not limited to zoning requests special use permits etc permit fee means any fee charged by the city for the issuance of a permit relating to construction demolition modification or improvement to property political subdivision means a county municipality special district school district junior college district housing authority or other political subdivision as such may be defined in the statutes of the state 01   waiver of fees a the city may waive administrative fees permit fees or both for political subdivisions political subdivisions shall remain responsible to the city for any costs required to be paid to third parties for the review of proposed plans to ensure compliance with the citys zoning requirements and building codes b upon written application to the city by the political subdivision the city shall make a determination on whether to grant a waiver of the fees described in subsection a of this section such waiver of administrative fees permit fees or both shall be made at the discretion of the city manager of the city the city manager shall provide a written response to the political subdivision requesting the waiver and in such response the city manager shall issue a finding granting denying or granting in part and denying in part the application for waiver 02   chapter 156  recreational vehicles purpose the purpose of this chapter is to establish regulations pertaining to recreational vehicles and recreational vehicle parks in the city and thereby promote community health and safety expansion or addition to any preexisting recreational vehicle parks will require the total recreational park to comply with this chapter  982011 definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this chapter shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning agent means any person authorized by the licensee of a recreational vehicle park to operate or maintain such park under the provisions of this chapter building official means the legally designated inspection authority of the city or his authorized representative as designated by the city manager certificate of occupancy means a certificate issued by the building official for the use of a building structure andor land when it is determined by him that the building structure andor land complies with the provisions of all applicable city codes ordinances and regulations city official means the director of public works permit director or other legally designated person of a city department or his authorized representative when acting in an official capacity or as designated by the city manager common access route means a private or public access roadway which affords the principal means of access to individual sites or auxiliary buildings the term common access route when used for emergency vehicles access shall meet minimum standards minimum standards shall equal or exceed six inches of crushed andor compacted base and further comply with the county andor city whichever is the more restrictive crushed and or compacted base means a minimum of six inches of flexible base compacted to 95 percent maximum density as determined by state department of transportations standard laboratory test procedure tex113e subgrade shall be moisture conditioned and compacted to 90 percent maximum density the flexible base material shall be item 200 type b flexible base as per city of san antonio standard specifications for construction or approved equal driveway means a minor entranceway off the common access route within the park into an offstreet parking area serving no more than two sites fire equipment means equipment specified by the nfpa as suitable for rv parks per nfpa standards hardsurface road means the minimum standards for the common access route or an asphalt or concrete road meeting the approval of the director of public works internal street means the same as common access route license means a written license issued by the building official permitting a person to operate and maintain a recreational vehicle park under the provisions of this chapter licensee means any person licensed to operate and maintain a recreational vehicle park under the provisions of this chapter park means a recreational vehicle park plot plan means a complete set of signed and sealed engineered drawings providing a graphic representation drawn to scale in a horizontal plane delineating the outlines of the land included in the plan and all proposed use locations accurately dimensioned with the dimensions also indicating the relation of each plane of use to that adjoining use and to the boundary of the property furthermore the drawing shall include a complete set of all utility road plans and existing and proposed improvement details private street means the same as the term common access route recreational vehicle means a portable home designed as a temporary dwelling for travel and recreational and vacation uses such homes shall not exceed eight feet in width and 46 feet in length and shall be classified as a recreational vehicle whether or not its wheels rollers skids or other rolling equipment have been removed and whether or not any addition thereto has been built on the ground  and such designations shall also include pickup campers converted buses selfpowered motor homes tent trailers tents and any temporary vehicular housing the term recreational vehicle specifically excludes modular office buildings tents and temporary dwellings modular buildings may not be located within a recreational vehicle park recreational vehicle park means a contiguous parcel of land licensed or used in whole or in part with or without charges for the parking of recreational vehicles occupied or intended to be occupied for dwelling or sleeping purposes for any length of time service building means a structure or housing toilets lavatories and such other facilities as may be required by this chapter sewer connection means the connection consisting of all pipes fittings and appurtenances from the drain outlet of a recreational vehicle to the inlet of the corresponding sewer service riser pipe of the sewage system serving the park or an individual site or pad sewer service riser pipe means the portion of a sewer service which extends vertically to the ground elevation and terminates at each site site plan means the same as the term plot plan space means a plot or pad of ground within the park designed for the accommodation of one recreational vehicle together with such parking and open space as required by this chapter the term space shall also include the terms lot stand or pad tow vehicle means a vehicle used to tow a recreational vehicle or a vehicle being towed by a recreational vehicle water connection means the connection consisting of all pipes fittings and appurtenances from the water riser pipe to the water inlet pipe of the distribution system within a recreational vehicle water riser pipe means the portion of the water service system serving a recreational vehicle park which extends vertically to the ground elevation and terminates at a designated point at a space  982011 general provisions a it shall be unlawful for any person for any reason to park or place a recreational vehicle within the city for a period longer than 72 hours the provisions of this chapter shall not however apply to 1 locations where recreational vehicles are manufactured andor sold or stored by the manufacturer or seller 2 a recreational vehicle located on a space in a recreational vehicle park duly licensed under the provisions of this chapter 3 locations where the city manager has granted a request to temporarily place recreational vehicles the request shall be in written form signed by the property owner requesting a specified period of time for the recreational vehicle to be present it shall also address how utilities will be supplied to the recreational vehicle if applicable with the request there shall also be provided a site plan showing the proposed location of recreational vehicles and any other structures on the property the city manager shall be cognizant of designated national emergencies which may require temporary flexibility and exceptions to this chapter 4 a personalindividual recreational vehicle located on an individuals personal property and the recreational vehicle provided it is not used as living quarters or storage b in any event a recreational vehicle shall not be parked on any street or parkway for the purpose of storage  982011 license it shall be unlawful for any person to maintain or operate a recreational vehicle park within the corporate limits of the city unless such person shall first obtain a license 1 license fees a the annual license fee for each recreational vehicle park shall be as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time b the fee for transfer of license shall be as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time license transfers will not be approved unless the recreational vehicle park is in compliance with the recreational vehicle park ordinance in effect at the time the original recreational vehicle park permit was approved c recreational vehicles are not allowed inside a manufactured home park and vice versa 2 application for license a application for recreational vehicle license shall be filed with the building official of the city and upon payment of the license fee recommendation by the planning and zoning commission of the city and upon formal approval by the city council the building official shall issue the license b applications shall be in writing signed by the applicant or a duly authorized officer or agent of applicant and shall contain at least the following 1 the name address email address and telephone number of the applicant  2 the location and legal description of the recreational vehicle park  3 complete set of engineered drawings drawn to scale and detailing the plans and specifications of the park drawn including all improvements constructed or to be constructed utility and street improvements  4 ingress and egress permits from the applicable state county city regulatory agency c such further information as may be requested by the planning and zoning commission to enable it to determine if the recreational vehicle park will comply with legal requirements  982011 location recreational vehicle parks may be located only in an area zoned for such use under the provisions of chapter 153 areas zoned for such use are herein designated by the city council as being special use  982011 recreational vehicle park plan a the recreational vehicle park shall conform to the following requirements 1 the park shall be located on a welldrained site properly graded and equipped to ensure rapid drainage and to be free from stagnant pools of water the condition of the soil groundwater drainage and topography shall be such that it shall not create a hazard to the property or the health and safety of the occupants no vehicle park will be allowed within the fema flood hazard area 2 each park shall provide recreational vehicle parking spaces and each such space shall be clearly defined rv parking spaces shall be not less than 18 feet by 50 feet and include auto parking spaces there must be at least a tenfoot clearance of space between the parked recreational vehicles if there is a conflict with any other provision of this this section shall control 3 the entrance to the park shall be designed to minimize congestion and hazards and allow free movement of traffic on adjacent streets and be approved by the appropriate state county and city agency 4 common access routes must be adequate to provide access to each recreational vehicle space and shall be constructed and maintained in good condition by the licensee and the width of which shall be not less than 24 feet the minimum inside radius of street intersections shall be 15 feet culdesacs streets longer than 150 feet will provide a minimum diameter of 100 feet of turning radius to accommodate emergency vehicles 5 the park shall comply with state and federal standards for accessible for the mobility impaired as it may be applicable the applicant shall show proof of compliance 6 no permanent fixtures will be permitted to be attached to the individual recreational vehicle spaces 7 any nonpermanent storage building andor units located on individual recreational vehicle spaces must be located a minimum of ten feet from the nearest recreational vehicle or other nonpermanent storage buildings andor units 8 only one recreational vehicle will be permitted in one recreational vehicle space b recreational vehicle stands or pads shall 1 be improved with a minimum of six inches of compacted crushed road base material or with asphalt or concrete adequate to support the weight of the recreational vehicle 2 not heave shift or settle unevenly under the weight of the recreational vehicle due to frost action inadequate drainage vibration or other forces acting on the structure c each parking space or pad shall be equipped with water sewer and electrical hook ups including onsite fire equipment which shall conform to all applicable codes or ordinances of the city and as detailed in the approved engineered drawings d all street and walkways shall be lighted at night light standards shall have a height and spacing to ensure an average illumination level of not less than 02 footcandles e all recreational vehicle spaces must provide for off street parking the parking space must be improved with a minimum of six inches of compacted crushed road base material or with asphalt or concrete adequate to support the weight of the vehicle  982011 garbage receptacles a each recreational vehicle park shall provide fly tight watertight rodent proof dumpsters to accommodate and provide a minimum of 90 gallons per recreational vehicle located within the recreational vehicle park at any given time there are approximately 202 gallons per cubic yard b the storage collection and disposal of refuse in the recreational vehicle park shall be so conducted as to create no health hazards  982011 fuels a bottled gas for cooking purposes shall not be used at individual recreational vehicle spaces unless the containers are properly connected by copper or other suitable metallic tubing and as designed by the recreational vehicles manufacturer b bottled gas cylinders shall be securely fastened in place as designed by the recreational vehicles manufacturer c no cylinders containing bottled gas shall be located in a recreational vehicle or within five feet of a door thereof d state and local regulations applicable to the handling of bottled gas and fuel oil shall apply e all applicable provisions of the ordinances of this city regulating the use of liquefied gas must be followed  982011 fire protection a general every park shall be equipped at all times with fire extinguishing equipment in good working order of such type size and number and so located within the park as to satisfy the national fire protection association nfpa dry fire extinguisher standards as may be modified by local purchase and inspection requirements acceptable to the fire chief the minimum number of approved fire extinguishers shall be at least equal to the number of recreational vehicles located within the recreational vehicle park the required number of fire extinguishers will be inclusive of the fire extinguishers located within the individual recreational vehicles located within the park b open fires prohibited no open fires shall be permitted except that this shall not be construed to prevent outside cooking andor barbecuing with natural gas in an approved closed pit or grill outside cooking or barbecuing with charcoal is prohibited c proximity to common access routes all sites and any part of a recreational vehicle shall not exceed 150 feet from the common access routes d storage and handling of flammable liquids only bottled gas for cooking shall be stored onsite e access to sites for firefighting approaches to all sites shall be regulated by the national fire radius requirements all sites shall be kept clear for firefighting personnel and equipment f firefighting instruction the park owner or agent shall be responsible for the instruction of his staff in the use of the park fire protection equipment and in their specific duties in the event of fire g water supply facilities for fire department operations 1 water supply facilities for fire department operations shall be connected to the city public water supply system 2 the park owner shall provide standard city approved fire hydrants located within 500 feet of all sites measured along the path of travel using driveways andor streets when fire hydrants are required the water mains and fire hydrants shall be dedicated to the city after construction of improvements is preformed to the city engineering standards and approved by the director of public works the water mains and fire hydrants when located on private property shall be in dedicated utility easements of the size set by the director of public works adequate to service said lines and hydrants after all development has accrued h dry vegetation the park licensee or agent shall be responsible for maintaining the entire area of the park free of dry brush leaves and weeds  982011 supervision a the attendant or caretaker shall be answerable with the licensee for the violation of any provision of this chapter to which the licensee is subject b the licensee or agent shall operate the park in compliance with this chapter and other applicable ordinances and shall provide adequate supervision to maintain the park its facilities and its equipment in good repair and in a clean and sanitary condition c the licensee or agent shall notify park occupants of all applicable provisions of this chapter and inform them of their duties and responsibilities under this chapter  982011 inspection a the building official building inspector the fire chief and the police chief are hereby authorized and directed to make such inspections as necessary to determine compliance with this chapter b the building official building inspector the fire chief and the police chief shall have the power to enter at reasonable times upon any private or public property for the purpose of inspecting conditions relating to the enforcement of this chapter c the building official building inspector fire chief and police chief shall have the power and authority in discharging their official duties to inspect the recreational vehicle park for compliance with this chapter and other safety and soundness issues  982011 revocation of license a the city manager may refuse to renew or seek to revoke any license to maintain and operate a park when the licensee has been found guilty by a court of competent jurisdiction of violating any provision of this chapter b after such conviction a new license may be reissued if the circumstances leading to conviction have been remedied and the park is being maintained and operated in full compliance with the law  982011 exceptions notwithstanding any of the requirements of this chapter if it be shown to the satisfaction of the planning and zoning commission that any of the requirements if complied with would cause undue hardship on any applicant for a license hereunder or licensee hereunder and that such requirement or requirements would not be for the best interest and general welfare of the city and the citizens affected by this chapter the planning and zoning commission may recommend to the city managercouncil waive such requirement or requirements  982011 appendix a  fee schedule footnotes  1  editors note printed herein is the fee schedule ordinance of the city as adopted by the city council on  amendments to the ordinance are
